href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a><sup id="cite_ref-law_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-law-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" Danger</a></span></div></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below noprint selfref" style="background-color:#E7E7FF;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;"><b>This article of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Greenlandic</b> (Greenlandic: <i lang="kl">kalaallisut</i> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="kl-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greenlandic" title="Help:IPA/Greenlandic">&#91;kalaːɬːisʉt&#93;</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <i lang="da">grønlandsk</i> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="da-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Danish" title="Help:IPA/Danish">&#91;ˈkʁɶnˌlænˀsk&#93;</a></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Eskimo%E2%80%93Aleut_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Eskimo–Aleut languages">Eskimo–Aleut language</a> with about 57,000 speakers,<sup id="cite_ref-e25_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e25-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> mostly <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_Inuit" title="Greenlandic Inuit">Greenlandic Inuit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>. It is closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Inuit_languages" title="Inuit languages">Inuit languages</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Inuktitut" title="Inuktitut">Inuktitut</a>. It is the most widely spoken Eskimo–Aleut language. In June 2009, the government of Greenland, the <a href="/wiki/Naalakkersuisut" title="Naalakkersuisut">Naalakkersuisut</a>, made Greenlandic the sole <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the autonomous territory, to strengthen it in the face of competition from the <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_imperialism" title="Linguistic imperialism">colonial language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>. The main <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">variety</a> is <a href="/wiki/West_Greenlandic" title="West Greenlandic">Kalaallisut</a>, or West Greenlandic. The second variety is <a href="/wiki/Tunumiit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunumiit language">Tunumiit oraasiat</a>, or East Greenlandic. The language of the <a href="/wiki/Inughuit" title="Inughuit">Inughuit</a> (Thule Inuit) of Greenland, <a href="/wiki/Inuktun" title="Inuktun">Inuktun</a> or Polar Eskimo, is a recent arrival and a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Inuktitut" title="Inuktitut">Inuktitut</a>.
</p><p>Greenlandic is a <a href="/wiki/Polysynthetic_language" title="Polysynthetic language">polysynthetic language</a> that allows the creation of long words by stringing together <a href="/wiki/Root_(linguistics)" title="Root (linguistics)">roots</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffixes</a>. The language's <a href="/wiki/Morphosyntactic_alignment" title="Morphosyntactic alignment">morphosyntactic alignment</a> is <a href="/wiki/Ergative%E2%80%93absolutive_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ergative–absolutive language">ergative</a>, treating both the argument (subject) of an intransitive verb and the <i>object</i> of a transitive verb in one way, but the <i>subject</i> of a transitive verb in another. For example, "<b>he</b> plays the guitar" would be in the ergative case as a transitive agent, whereas "I bought a <b>guitar</b>" and "as the <b>guitar</b> plays" (the latter being the intransitive sense of the same verb "to play") would both be in the absolutive case.
</p><p>Nouns are inflected by one of eight <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">cases</a> and for possession. <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">Verbs</a> are inflected for one of eight <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">moods</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">person</a> of its <a href="/wiki/Subject_(grammar)" title="Subject (grammar)">subject</a> and <a href="/wiki/Object_(grammar)" title="Object (grammar)">object</a>. Both nouns and verbs have complex derivational morphology. The basic <a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">word order</a> in <a href="/wiki/Transitivity_(grammar)" title="Transitivity (grammar)">transitive</a> <a href="/wiki/Clause" title="Clause">clauses</a> is <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93object%E2%80%93verb" class="mw-redirect" title="Subject–object–verb">subject–object–verb</a>. The subordination of clauses uses special subordinate moods. A so-called fourth-person category enables <a href="/wiki/Switch-reference" title="Switch-reference">switch-reference</a> between main clauses and subordinate clauses with different subjects. Greenlandic is notable for its lack of <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">grammatical tense</a>; temporal relations are expressed normally by context but also by the use of temporal particles such as "yesterday" or "now" or sometimes by the use of derivational suffixes or the combination of affixes with <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">aspectual</a> meanings with the semantic <a href="/wiki/Lexical_aspect" title="Lexical aspect">lexical aspect</a> of different verbs. However, some linguists have suggested that Greenlandic always marks <a href="/wiki/Future_tense" title="Future tense">future tense</a>. Another question is whether the language has <a href="/wiki/Noun_incorporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Noun incorporation">noun incorporation</a> or whether the processes that create complex predicates that include nominal roots are derivational in nature.
</p><p>When adopting new concepts or technologies, Greenlandic usually constructs new words made from Greenlandic roots, but modern Greenlandic has also taken many <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loans</a> from Danish and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>. The language has been written in <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> since Danish colonization began in the 1700s. Greenlandic's first <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">orthography</a> was developed by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Kleinschmidt" title="Samuel Kleinschmidt">Samuel Kleinschmidt</a> in 1851, but within 100 years, it already differed substantially from the <a href="/wiki/Spoken_language" title="Spoken language">spoken language</a> because of a number of <a href="/wiki/Sound_changes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sound changes">sound changes</a>. An extensive <a href="/wiki/Orthographic_reform" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthographic reform">orthographic reform</a> was undertaken in 1973 and made the <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">script</a> much easier to learn. This resulted in a boost in Greenlandic <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a>, which is now among the <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate by country">highest in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg/350px-Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="313" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg/525px-Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg/700px-Inuktitut_dialect_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="798" data-file-height="714" /></a><figcaption>Illustration 1: Distribution of Inuit language variants across the Arctic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This image needs references to reliable sources (November 2022)">image reference needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Greenlandic was brought to Greenland by the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a> in the 1200s. The languages that were spoken by the earlier <a href="/wiki/Saqqaq_culture" title="Saqqaq culture">Saqqaq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset cultures</a> in Greenland are unknown.
</p><p>The first descriptions of Greenlandic date from the 1600s. With the arrival of Danish missionaries in the early 1700s and the beginning of Danish colonization of Greenland, the compilation of dictionaries and description of grammar began. The missionary <a href="/wiki/Paul_Egede" title="Paul Egede">Paul Egede</a> wrote the first Greenlandic dictionary in 1750 and the first grammar in 1760.<sup id="cite_ref-encyc_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From the Danish colonization in the 1700s to the beginning of Greenlandic home rule in 1979, Greenlandic experienced increasing pressure from the Danish language. In the 1950s, Denmark's linguistic policies were directed at strengthening Danish. Of primary significance was the fact that post-primary education and official functions were conducted in Danish.<sup id="cite_ref-SocEd_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SocEd-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1851 to 1973, Greenlandic was written in a complicated orthography devised by the missionary linguist <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Kleinschmidt" title="Samuel Kleinschmidt">Samuel Kleinschmidt</a>. In 1973, a new orthography was introduced, intended to bring the written language closer to the spoken standard, which had changed considerably since Kleinschmidt's time. The reform was effective, and in the years following it, Greenlandic literacy has received a boost.<sup id="cite_ref-SocEd_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SocEd-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another development that has strengthened Greenlandic language is the policy of "Greenlandization" of Greenlandic society that began with the home rule agreement of 1979. The policy has worked to reverse the former trend towards marginalization of the Greenlandic language by making it the official language of education. The fact that Greenlandic has become the only language used in primary schooling means that monolingual Danish-speaking parents in Greenland are now raising children bilingual in Danish and Greenlandic.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Greenlandic now has several dedicated news media: the Greenlandic National Radio, <a href="/wiki/Kalaallit_Nunaata_Radioa" title="Kalaallit Nunaata Radioa">Kalaallit Nunaata Radioa</a>, which provides television and radio programming in Greenlandic. The newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Sermitsiaq_(newspaper)" title="Sermitsiaq (newspaper)">Sermitsiaq</a></i> has been published since 1958 and merged in 2010 with the other newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Atuagagdliutit/Gr%C3%B8nlandsposten" title="Atuagagdliutit/Grønlandsposten">Atuagagdliutit/Grønlandsposten</a></i>, which had been established in 1861 to form a single large Greenlandic language publishing house.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before June 2009, Greenlandic shared its status as the official language in Greenland with Danish.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Greenlandic has become the sole official language.<sup id="cite_ref-law_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-law-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> That has made Greenlandic a unique example of an <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">indigenous language of the Americas</a> that is recognized by law as the only official language of a semi-independent country. Nevertheless, it is still considered to be in a "vulnerable" state by the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Red_Book_of_Endangered_Languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Book of Endangered Languages">Red Book of Language Endangerment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The country has a 100% literacy rate.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As the Western Greenlandic standard has become dominant, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> report has labelled the other dialects as endangered, and measures are now being considered to protect the Eastern Greenlandic dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/West_Greenlandic" title="West Greenlandic">Kalaallisut</a> and the other Greenlandic dialects belong to the <a href="/wiki/Eskimo%E2%80%93Aleut_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Eskimo–Aleut languages">Eskimo–Aleut family</a> and are closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Inuit_languages" title="Inuit languages">Inuit languages</a> of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>. Illustration 1 shows the locations of the different Inuit languages, among them the two main dialects of Greenlandic and the separate language Inuktun ("Avanersuaq").
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; clear: right;">
<caption>Example of differences between the 3 main dialects
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>English
</th>
<th>Kalaallisut
</th>
<th>Inuktun
</th>
<th>Tunumiisut
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>humans
</td>
<td><i>inuit</i>
</td>
<td><i>inughuit</i><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><i>iivit</i><sup id="cite_ref-Mennecier_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mennecier-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The most prominent Greenlandic dialect is Kalaallisut, which is the official language of Greenland. The name <i>Kalaallisut</i> is often used as a cover term for all of Greenlandic. The eastern dialect <i>(<a href="/wiki/Tunumiit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunumiit language">Tunumiit oraasiat</a>)</i>, spoken in the vicinity of <a href="/wiki/Ammassalik_Island" title="Ammassalik Island">Ammassalik Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ittoqqortoormiit" title="Ittoqqortoormiit">Ittoqqortoormiit</a>, is the most innovative of the Greenlandic dialects since it has <a href="/wiki/Assimilation_(phonology)" title="Assimilation (phonology)">assimilated</a> <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">consonant clusters</a> and vowel sequences more than West Greenlandic.<sup id="cite_ref-MahieuTersis_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MahieuTersis-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kalaallisut is further divided into four subdialects. One that is spoken around <a href="/wiki/Upernavik" title="Upernavik">Upernavik</a> has certain similarities to East Greenlandic, possibly because of a previous migration from eastern Greenland. A second dialect is spoken in the region of <a href="/wiki/Uummannaq" title="Uummannaq">Uummannaq</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Disko_Bay" title="Disko Bay">Disko Bay</a>. The standard language is based on the central Kalaallisut dialect spoken in <a href="/wiki/Sisimiut" title="Sisimiut">Sisimiut</a> in the north, around <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a> and as far south as <a href="/wiki/Maniitsoq" title="Maniitsoq">Maniitsoq</a>. Southern Kalaallisut is spoken around <a href="/wiki/Narsaq" title="Narsaq">Narsaq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qaqortoq" title="Qaqortoq">Qaqortoq</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-encyc_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Table 1 shows the differences in the pronunciation of the word for "humans" in the two main dialects and Inuktun. It can be seen that Inuktun is the most conservative by maintaining <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;gh&#x27e9;</span>, which has been elided in Kalaallisut, and Tunumiisut is the most innovative by further simplifying its structure by eliding <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<th><a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">Close</a>
</th>
<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">i</a></span> (<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close_front_rounded_vowel" title="Close front rounded vowel">y</a></span>)
</td>
<td>(<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close_central_rounded_vowel" title="Close central rounded vowel">ʉ</a></span>)
</td>
<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">u</a></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Mid_vowel" title="Mid vowel">Mid</a>
</th>
<td colspan="2">(<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">e</a></span>~<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">ɛ</a></span>~<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Near-open_central_vowel" title="Near-open central vowel">ɐ</a></span>)
</td>
<td>(<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">o</a></span>~<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">ɔ</a></span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Open_vowel" title="Open vowel">Open</a>
</th>
<td colspan="2"><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">a</a></span>
</td>
<td>(<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">ɑ</a></span>)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg/220px-West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg/330px-West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg/440px-West_Greenlandic_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="713" /></a><figcaption>Ranges of West Greenlandic monophthongs on a <a href="/wiki/Vowel_chart" class="mw-redirect" title="Vowel chart">vowel chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>The Greenlandic three-<a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowel</a> system, composed of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span>, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span>, is typical for an Eskimo–Aleut language. Double vowels are analyzed as two <a href="/wiki/Mora_(linguistics)" title="Mora (linguistics)">morae</a> and so they are phonologically a vowel sequence and not a long vowel. They are also orthographically written as two vowels.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jacobsen_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacobsen-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> There is only one diphthong, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ai/</span>, which occurs only at the ends of words.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Before a <a href="/wiki/Uvular_consonant" title="Uvular consonant">uvular consonant</a> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/q/</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁ/</span>), <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> is realized <a href="/wiki/Allophonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Allophonic">allophonically</a> as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[e]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛ]</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɐ]</span>, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> is realized <a href="/wiki/Allophonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Allophonic">allophonically</a> as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[o]</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɔ]</span>, and the two vowels are written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e, o&#x27e9;</span> respectively (as in some orthographies used for <a href="/wiki/Quechuan_languages" title="Quechuan languages">Quechua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-NTNU_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTNU-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> becomes retracted to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑ]</span> in the same environment. <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> is rounded to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[y]</span> before labial consonants.<sup id="cite_ref-NTNU_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTNU-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> is fronted to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʉ]</span> between two coronal consonants.<sup id="cite_ref-NTNU_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTNU-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The allophonic lowering of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> before uvular consonants is shown in the modern orthography by writing <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> as <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e&#x27e9;</span> and <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;o&#x27e9;</span> respectively before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;q&#x27e9;</span> and <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;r&#x27e9;</span>. For example:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ui/</span> "husband" pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ui]</span>.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uiqarpuq/</span> "(s)he has a husband" pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ueqɑppɔq]</span> and written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ueqarpoq&#x27e9;</span>.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/illu/</span> "house" pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iɬɬu]</span>.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/illuqarpuq/</span> "(s)he has a house" pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iɬɬoqɑppɔq]</span> and written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;illoqarpoq&#x27e9;</span>.</li></ul>

<p>The palatal sibilant <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʃ]</span> has merged with <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[s]</span> in all dialects except those of the <a href="/wiki/Sisimiut" title="Sisimiut">Sisimiut</a>–<a href="/wiki/Maniitsoq" title="Maniitsoq">Maniitsoq</a>–<a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>–<a href="/wiki/Paamiut" title="Paamiut">Paamiut</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The labiodental fricative <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[f]</span> is contrastive only in <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a>. The alveolar stop <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span> is pronounced as an affricate <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t͡s]</span> before the high front vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>. Often, Danish loanwords containing <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;b d g&#x27e9;</span> preserve these in writing, but that does not imply a change in pronunciation, for example <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;baaja&#x27e9;</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[paːja]</span> "beer" and <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;Guuti&#x27e9;</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kuːtˢi]</span> "God"; these are pronounced exactly as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p<span class="wrap"> </span>t<span class="wrap"> </span>k/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-encyc2_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc2-32">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">Morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Morphology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg/350px-Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="263" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg/525px-Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/62/Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>A bilingual sign in Nuuk showing the contrast between Danish and Kalaallisut. The sign translates to "parking forbidden for all vehicles."</figcaption></figure>
<p>The broad outline of the Greenlandic grammar is similar to other Eskimo languages, on the morpholological and syntactic plan.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphology</a> of Greenlandic is highly <a href="/wiki/Polysynthetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Polysynthetic">synthetic</a> and exclusively suffixing<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> (except for a single highly-limited and fossilized demonstrative prefix). The language creates very long words by means of adding strings of suffixes to a stem.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> In principle, there is no limit to the length of a Greenlandic word, but in practice, words with more than six derivational suffixes are not so frequent, and the average number of morphemes per word is three to five.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> The language has between 400 and 500 derivational suffixes and around 318 inflectional suffixes.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are few compound words but many derivations.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The grammar uses a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Head-marking_language" title="Head-marking language">head</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dependent-marking_language" title="Dependent-marking language">dependent marking</a>. Both <a href="/wiki/Agent_(grammar)" title="Agent (grammar)">agent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patient_(grammar)" title="Patient (grammar)">patient</a> are marked on the predicate, and the possessor is marked on nouns, with dependent <a href="/wiki/Noun_phrases" class="mw-redirect" title="Noun phrases">noun phrases</a> inflecting for case. The primary <a href="/wiki/Morphosyntactic_alignment" title="Morphosyntactic alignment">morphosyntactic alignment</a> of full noun phrases in Kalaallisut is <a href="/wiki/Ergative_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ergative language">ergative-absolutive</a>, but verbal morphology follows a <a href="/wiki/Nominative%E2%80%93accusative_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominative–accusative language">nominative-accusative</a> pattern and pronouns are syntactically neutral.
</p><p>The language distinguishes four persons (1st, 2nd, 3rd and 4th or 3rd reflexive (see <a href="#Obviation_and_switch-reference">Obviation and switch-reference</a>); two numbers (singular and plural but no <a href="/wiki/Dual_(grammatical_number)" title="Dual (grammatical number)">dual</a>, unlike Inuktitut); eight moods (indicative, interrogative, imperative, optative, conditional, causative, contemporative and participial) and eight cases (absolutive, ergative, equative, instrumental, locative, allative, ablative and prolative). Greenlandic (including the eastern  Tunumiisut variety) is the only Eskimo language having lost its dual.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Declension">Declension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Declension"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<th>Ablative
</th>
<td>+mit
</td>
<td>+nit
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Locative
</th>
<td>+mi
</td>
<td>+ni
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Prolative
</th>
<td>+kkut
</td>
<td>+tigut
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Equative
</th>
<td colspan="2">+tut
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Verbs carry a bipersonal inflection for subject and object. Possessive noun phrases inflect for both possessor and case.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In this section, the examples are written in Greenlandic standard orthography except that morpheme boundaries are indicated by a hyphen.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">Syntax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Syntax"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Greenlandic distinguishes three <a href="/wiki/Open_class_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Open class (linguistics)">open word classes</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nouns" class="mw-redirect" title="Nouns">nouns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Verbs">verbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_particle" title="Grammatical particle">particles</a>. Verbs inflect for person and number of subject and object as well as for mood. Nouns inflect for possession and for case. Particles do not inflect.<sup id="cite_ref-Bjørnum_2003_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bjørnum_2003-40">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th>&#160;</th>
<th>Verb</th>
<th>Noun</th>
<th>Particle
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>Word
</th>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Oqar-poq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">say-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="indicative mood" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IND</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Oqar-poq</p><p style="display: none;">say-3SG/IND</p><p style="clear: left;">"he says"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Angut</p><p style="margin: 0px;">man.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="absolutive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABS</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Angut</p><p style="display: none;">man.ABS</p><p style="clear: left;">"A man"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Naamik</p><p style="margin: 0px;">No</p></div><p style="display: none;">Naamik</p><p style="display: none;">No</p><p style="clear: left;">"No"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The verb is the only word that is required in a sentence. Since verbs inflect for number and person of both subject and object, the verb is in fact a clause itself. Therefore, clauses in which all participants are expressed as free-standing noun phrases are rather rare.<sup id="cite_ref-Bjørnum_2003_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bjørnum_2003-40">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The following examples show the possibilities of leaving out the verbal arguments:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Intransitive clause with no subject noun phrase:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Sini-ppoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sleep-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="indicative mood" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IND</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Sini-ppoq</p><p style="display: none;">sleep-3SG/IND</p><p style="clear: left;">"(S)he sleeps"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Intransitive clause with subject noun phrase:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Angut</p><p style="margin: 0px;">man.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="absolutive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sinippoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sleep-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="indicative mood" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IND</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Angut sinippoq</p><p style="display: none;">man.ABS sleep-3SG/IND</p><p style="clear: left;">"the man sleeps"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Transitive clause with no overt arguments:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Asa-vaa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Asa-vaa</p><p style="display: none;">love-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"(S)he loves him/her/it"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Transitive clause with agent noun phrase:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Angut-ip</p><p style="margin: 0px;">man-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ergative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ERG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa-vaa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Angut-ip asa-vaa</p><p style="display: none;">man-ERG love-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"the man loves him/her/it"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Transitive clause with patient noun phrase:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Arnaq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">woman.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="absolutive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa-vaa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Arnaq asa-vaa</p><p style="display: none;">woman.ABS love-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"(S)he loves the woman"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Morphosyntactic_alignment">Morphosyntactic alignment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Morphosyntactic alignment"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Greenlandic language uses <a href="/wiki/Case_(grammar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Case (grammar)">case</a> to express grammatical relations between participants in a sentence. Nouns are inflected with one of the two core cases or one of the six oblique cases.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Greenlandic is an ergative–absolutive language and so instead of treating the <a href="/wiki/Morphosyntax" class="mw-redirect" title="Morphosyntax">grammatical relations</a>, as in English and most other <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a>, whose grammatical <a href="/wiki/Subject_(grammar)" title="Subject (grammar)">subjects</a> are marked with the nominative case and <a href="/wiki/Object_(grammar)" title="Object (grammar)">objects</a> with the accusative case, Greenlandic grammatical roles are defined differently. Its ergative case is used for <a href="/wiki/Agent_(grammar)" title="Agent (grammar)">agents</a> of transitive verbs and for possessors. The absolutive case is used for patients of transitive verbs and subjects of intransitive verbs.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Research into Greenlandic as used by the younger generation has shown that the use of ergative alignment in Kalaallisut may be becoming obsolete, which would convert the language into a <a href="/wiki/Nominative%E2%80%93accusative_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominative–accusative language">nominative–accusative language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Intransitive:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Anda</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="absolutive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sini-ppoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sleep-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="indicative mood" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IND</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Anda sini-ppoq</p><p style="display: none;">Anda.ABS sleep-3SG/IND</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda sleeps"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Transitive with agent and object:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Anda-p</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ergative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ERG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nanoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bear.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="absolutive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">taku-aa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Anda-p nanoq taku-aa</p><p style="display: none;">Anda-ERG bear.ABS see-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda sees a bear"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Word order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In transitive clauses whose object and subject are expressed as free noun phrases, the basic pragmatically-neutral word order is <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93object%E2%80%93verb" class="mw-redirect" title="Subject–object–verb">SOV / SOXV</a> in which X is a noun phrase in one of the oblique cases. However, word order is fairly free. <a href="/wiki/Topic_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Topic (linguistics)">Topical</a> noun phrases occur at the beginning of a clause. New or emphasized information generally come last, which is usually the verb but can also be a <a href="/wiki/Focus_(linguistics)" title="Focus (linguistics)">focal</a> subject or object. As well, in the spoken language, "afterthought" material or clarifications may follow the verb, usually in a lowered pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the other hand, the noun phrase is characterized by a rigid order in which the head of the phrase precedes any modifiers and the possessor precedes the possessed.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2022)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Copula_(linguistics)" title="Copula (linguistics)">copula</a> clauses, the word order is usually subject-copula-complement.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Andap</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda</p><p style="margin: 0px;">A</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tujuuluk</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sweater</p><p style="margin: 0px;">O</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pisiaraa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bought</p><p style="margin: 0px;">V</p></div><p style="display: none;">Andap tujuuluk pisiaraa</p><p style="display: none;">Anda sweater bought</p><p style="display: none;">A O V</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda bought the sweater"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>An attribute appears after its head noun.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Andap</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda</p><p style="margin: 0px;">A</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tujuuluk</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sweater</p><p style="margin: 0px;">O</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tungujortoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">blue</p><p style="margin: 0px;">X</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pisiaraa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bought</p><p style="margin: 0px;">V</p></div><p style="display: none;">Andap tujuuluk tungujortoq pisiaraa</p><p style="display: none;">Anda sweater blue bought</p><p style="display: none;">A O X V</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda bought the blue sweater"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>An attribute of an incorporated noun appears after the verb:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Anda</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda</p><p style="margin: 0px;">S</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sanasuuvoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">carpenter-is</p><p style="margin: 0px;">V</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pikkorissoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">skilled</p><p style="margin: 0px;">APP</p></div><p style="display: none;">Anda sanasuuvoq pikkorissoq</p><p style="display: none;">Anda {carpenter-is} skilled</p><p style="display: none;">S V APP</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda is a skilled carpenter"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coordination_and_subordination">Coordination and subordination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coordination and subordination"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Syntactic <a href="/wiki/Coordination_(linguistics)" title="Coordination (linguistics)">coordination</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subordination_(linguistics)" title="Subordination (linguistics)">subordination</a> is built by combining predicates in the superordinate moods (indicative, interrogative, imperative and optative) with predicates in the subordinate moods (conditional, causative, contemporative and participial). The contemporative has both coordinative and subordinative functions, depending on the context.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The relative order of the main clause and its coordinate or subordinate clauses is relatively free and is subject mostly to <a href="/wiki/Pragmatics" title="Pragmatics">pragmatic</a> concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Obviation_and_switch-reference">Obviation and switch-reference</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Obviation and switch-reference"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Greenlandic pronominal system includes a distinction known as <a href="/wiki/Obviative" title="Obviative">obviation</a><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Switch-reference" title="Switch-reference">switch-reference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> There is a special so-called fourth person<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> to denote a third person subject of a subordinate verb or the possessor of a noun that is coreferent with the third person subject of the matrix clause.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Here are examples of the difference between third and the fourth persons:
</p>
<blockquote>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">


<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<dl><dt>third person</dt></dl>
<div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">illu-<b>a</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">house-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessor" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">taku-aa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">illu-<b>a</b> taku-aa</p><p style="display: none;">house-3.POSS see-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"he saw his (the other man's) house"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ole</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Ole</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">oqar-poq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">say-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tillu-<b>kkiga</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">hit-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Ole oqar-poq tillu-<b>kkiga</b></p><p style="display: none;">Ole say-3SG hit-1SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"Ole said I had hit him (the other man)"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Eva</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Eva</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">iser-<b>pat</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">come in-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sini-ssaa-q</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sleep-expect-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Eva iser-<b>pat</b> sini-ssaa-q</p><p style="display: none;">Eva {come in}-3SG sleep-expect-3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"When Eva comes in (s)he'll sleep (someone else)"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<dl><dt>fourth person</dt></dl>
<div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">illu-<b>ni</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">house-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="fourth (reflexive or obviative) person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">4</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessor" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">taku-aa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">illu-<b>ni</b> taku-aa</p><p style="display: none;">house-4.POSS see-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"he saw his own house"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ole</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Ole</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">oqar-poq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">say-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tillu-<b>kkini</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">hit-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="fourth (reflexive or obviative) person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">4</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Ole oqar-poq tillu-<b>kkini</b></p><p style="display: none;">Ole say-3SG hit-1SG/4</p><p style="clear: left;">"Ole said I had hit him (Ole)"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>

</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indefiniteness_construction">Indefiniteness construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Indefiniteness construction"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There is no category of <a href="/wiki/Definiteness" title="Definiteness">definiteness</a> in Greenlandic and so information on whether participants are already known to the listener or they are new to the discourse is encoded by other means. According to some authors, morphology related to transitivity such as the use of the construction sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Antipassive_voice" title="Antipassive voice">antipassive</a><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sadock_2003_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sadock_2003-53">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> or intransitive object<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> conveys such meaning, along with strategies of noun incorporation of non-topical noun phrases.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> That view, however, is controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-Bittner_1987_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bittner_1987-57">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Active:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Piitap</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Peter-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ergative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ERG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">arfeq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">whale</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">takuaa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see</p></div><p style="display: none;">Piitap arfeq takuaa</p><p style="display: none;">Peter-ERG whale see</p><p style="clear: left;">"Peter saw the whale"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>Antipassive/intransitive object:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Piitaq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Peter-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="absolutive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">arfermik</p><p style="margin: 0px;">whale-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="instrumental case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INSTR</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">takuvoq</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see</p></div><p style="display: none;">Piitaq arfermik takuvoq</p><p style="display: none;">Peter-ABS whale-INSTR see</p><p style="clear: left;">"Peter saw (a) whale"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs">Verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The morphology of Greenlandic verbs is enormously complex. The main processes are <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflection</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derivation_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Derivation (linguistics)">derivation</a>. Inflectional morphology includes the processes of obligatory inflection for mood, person and <a href="/wiki/Voice_(grammar)" title="Voice (grammar)">voice</a> (tense and <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">aspect</a> are not inflectional categories in Kalaallisut).<sup id="cite_ref-Shaer_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaer-58">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bittner2005_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bittner2005-59">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HayashiSprenger_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HayashiSprenger-60">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Derivational morphology modifies the meaning of verbs similarly to English <a href="/wiki/Adverbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Adverbs">adverbs</a>. There are hundreds of such derivational suffixes. Many of them are so semantically salient and so they are often referred to as <a href="/wiki/Postbase" title="Postbase">postbases</a>, rather than suffixes, particularly in the American tradition of Eskimo grammar.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Such semantically "heavy" suffixes may express concepts such as "to have", "to be", "to say" or "to think". The Greenlandic verb word consists of a root, followed by derivational suffixes/postbases and then inflectional suffixes. Tense and aspect are marked by optional suffixes between the derivational and the inflectional suffixes.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflection">Inflection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Inflection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Greenlandic verbs inflect for <a href="/wiki/Agreement_(linguistics)" title="Agreement (linguistics)">agreement</a> with agent and patient and for mood and for voice. There are eight moods, four of which are used in independent clauses the others in subordinate clauses. The four independent moods are <a href="/wiki/Indicative" class="mw-redirect" title="Indicative">indicative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interrogative_mood" class="mw-redirect" title="Interrogative mood">interrogative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperative_mood" title="Imperative mood">imperative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Optative" class="mw-redirect" title="Optative">optative</a>. The four dependent moods are causative, conditional, contemporative and participial. Verbal roots can take transitive, intransitive or <a href="/wiki/Negation_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Negation (linguistics)">negative</a> inflections and so all eight mood suffixes have those three forms.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The inflectional system is even more complex since transitive suffixes encode both agent and patient in a single morpheme, with up to 48 different suffixes covering all possible combinations of agent and patient for each of the eight transitive paradigms. As some moods do not have forms for all persons (imperative has only 2nd person, optative has only 1st and 3rd person, participial mood has no 4th person and contemporative has no 3rd person), the total number of verbal inflectional suffixes is about 318.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Indicative_and_interrogative_moods">Indicative and interrogative moods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Indicative and interrogative moods"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The indicative mood is used in all independent expository clauses. The interrogative mood is used for <a href="/wiki/Question#Grammar" title="Question">questions</a> that do not have the question particle <i>immaqa</i> "maybe".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>interrogative mood:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">napparsima-vit?</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be sick-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="second person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">2</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="interrogative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INTERR</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">napparsima-vit?</p><p style="display: none;">{be sick}-2/INTERR</p><p style="clear: left;">"Are you sick?"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div><b>indicative mood:</b></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">naamik,</p><p style="margin: 0px;">no,</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">napparsima-nngila-nga</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be sick-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="negation/negative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">NEG</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="indicative mood" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IND</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">naamik, napparsima-nngila-nga</p><p style="display: none;">no, {be sick}-NEG-1/IND</p><p style="clear: left;">"No, I am not sick"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The table below shows the intransitive inflection of the verb <i>neri-</i> "to eat" in the indicative and interrogative moods (question marks mark interrogative intonation; questions have falling intonation on the last syllable, unlike English and most other Indo-European languages, whose questions are marked by rising intonation). Both the indicative and the interrogative mood have a transitive and an intransitive inflection, but only the intransitive inflection is given here. <a href="/wiki/Consonant_gradation" title="Consonant gradation">Consonant gradation</a> like in <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> appears to occur in the verb conjugation (with strengthening to <i>pp</i> in the 3rd person plural and weakening to <i>v</i> elsewhere).
</p>

</td>

</td></tr>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>nerivugut</i> "We are eating"
</td>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>nerivusi</i> "You are eating (pl.)"
</td>

<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vara</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vara</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-1SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"I love him/her/it"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vat</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="second person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">2SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vat</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-2SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"You love her/him/it"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vaa</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vaa</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"He/she/it loves him/her/it"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>*
</td>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vatsigut</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="second person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">2SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, plural" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vatsigut</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-2SG/1PL</p><p style="clear: left;">"You love us"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>

<tr>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vakka</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, plural" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vakka</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-1SG/3PL</p><p style="clear: left;">"I love them"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>

<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vatit</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="second person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">2SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, plural" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vatit</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-2SG/3PL</p><p style="clear: left;">"You love them"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td><div class="interlinear"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">asa<b>vai</b></p><p style="margin: 0px;">love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, plural" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">asa<b>vai</b></p><p style="display: none;">love-3SG/3PL</p><p style="clear: left;">"He/she/it loves them"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The table below gives the basic form of all the inflexional suffixes in the indicative and interrogative moods. Where the indicative and interrogative forms differ, the interrogative form is given second in brackets. Suffixes used with intransitive verbs are in <i>italics</i>, while suffixes used with transitive verbs are unmarked.
</p>
