<p>In Greenlandic, <a href="/wiki/Possession_(linguistics)" title="Possession (linguistics)">possession</a> is marked on the noun that agrees with the person and the number of its possessor. The possessor is in the ergative case. There are different possessive paradigms for each different case.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Table 4 gives the possessive paradigm for the absolutive case of <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">illu</i></span> "house". Here are examples of the use of the possessive inflection, the use of the ergative case for possessors and the use of fourth person possessors.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Anda-p</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ergative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ERG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">illu-a</p><p style="margin: 0px;">house-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessor" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Anda-p illu-a</p><p style="display: none;">Anda-ERG house-3SG/POSS</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda's house"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Anda-p</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ergative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ERG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">illu-ni</p><p style="margin: 0px;">house-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="fourth (reflexive or obviative) person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">4</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessor" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">taku-aa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Anda-p illu-ni taku-aa</p><p style="display: none;">Anda-ERG house-4/POSS see-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda sees his own house"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">ex:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Anda-p</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Anda-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ergative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ERG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">illu-a</p><p style="margin: 0px;">house-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessor" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kl" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">taku-aa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">see-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr>/<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Anda-p illu-a taku-aa</p><p style="display: none;">Anda-ERG house-3SG/POSS see-3SG/3SG</p><p style="clear: left;">"Anda sees his (the other man's) house"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Numerals">Numerals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Numerals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The numerals and lower numbers are,<sup id="cite_ref-Dorais_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorais-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilimmarfik.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ilimmarfik.jpg/220px-Ilimmarfik.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ilimmarfik.jpg/330px-Ilimmarfik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ilimmarfik.jpg/440px-Ilimmarfik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="448" data-file-height="336" /></a><figcaption>The orthography and the vocabulary of the Greenlandic language is governed by <i>Oqaasileriffik</i>, the Greenlandic language secretariat, located in the <i>Ilimmarfik</i> university campus in <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Most of Greenlandic's <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">vocabulary</a> is inherited from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Eskimo%E2%80%93Aleut" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Eskimo–Aleut">Proto-Eskimo–Aleut</a>, but there are also a large number of loans from other languages, especially from Danish. Early loans from Danish have often become acculturated to the Greenlandic phonological system: the Greenlandic word <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">palasi</i></span> "priest" is a loan from the Danish <span title="Danish-language text"><i lang="da">præst</i></span>. However, since Greenlandic has an enormous potential for the derivation of new words from existing roots, many modern concepts have Greenlandic names that have been invented rather than borrowed: <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">qarasaasiaq</i></span> "computer" which literally means "artificial brain". The potential for complex derivations also means that Greenlandic vocabulary is built on very few roots, which, combined with affixes, form large word families.<sup id="cite_ref-encyc_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> For example, the root for "tongue" <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaq</i></span> is used to derive the following words:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqarpoq</i></span> 'says'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaaseq</i></span> 'word'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaluppoq</i></span> 'speaks'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqallissaarut</i></span> 'discussion paper'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaasilerisoq</i></span> 'linguist'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaasilerissutit</i></span> 'grammar'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaluttualiortoq</i></span> 'author'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaloqatigiinneq</i></span> 'conversation'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaasipiluuppaa</i></span> 'harangues him'</li>
<li><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">oqaatiginerluppaa</i></span> 'speaks badly about him'</li></ul>
<p>Lexical differences between dialects are often considerable because of the earlier cultural practice of imposing a <a href="/wiki/Taboo" title="Taboo">taboo</a> on words that had served as names for a deceased person. Since people were often named after everyday objects, many of them have changed their name several times because of taboo rules, another cause of the divergence of dialectal vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-encyc_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_(ubt).JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_%28ubt%29.JPG/220px-%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_%28ubt%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_%28ubt%29.JPG/330px-%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_%28ubt%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_%28ubt%29.JPG/440px-%C4%B8ra_in_a_dictionary_%28ubt%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption><b><a href="/wiki/Kra_(letter)" title="Kra (letter)"><span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ĸ&#x27e9;</span></a></b> in a Greenlandic–Danish dictionary from 1926</figcaption></figure><p>Greenlandic is written with the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Alphabet" title="Alphabet">alphabet</a> consists of 18 <a href="/wiki/Letter_(alphabet)" title="Letter (alphabet)">letters</a>:
</p><ul><li>A E F G I J K L M N O P Q R S T U V</li></ul>
<p><span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;b, c, d, h, w, x, y, z, æ, ø, å&#x27e9;</span> are used to spell loanwords, especially from Danish and English.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Greenlandic uses "..." and&#160;»...«&#160;as <a href="/wiki/Non-English_usage_of_quotation_marks" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-English usage of quotation marks">quotation marks</a>.
</p><p>From 1851 until 1973, Greenlandic was written in an alphabet invented by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Kleinschmidt" title="Samuel Kleinschmidt">Samuel Kleinschmidt</a>, which used the <i><a href="/wiki/Kra_(letter)" title="Kra (letter)">kra</a></i> (<span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ĸ&#x27e9;</span>, capitalised <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;K’&#x27e9;</span>) which was replaced by <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;<a href="/wiki/Q" title="Q">q</a>&#x27e9;</span> in the 1973 <a href="/wiki/Spelling_reform" title="Spelling reform">reform</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In the Kleinschmidt alphabet, <a href="/wiki/Long_vowels" class="mw-redirect" title="Long vowels">long vowels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geminate_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Geminate consonant">geminate consonants</a> were indicated by <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a> on vowels (in the case of consonant gemination, the diacritics were placed on the vowel preceding the affected consonant). For example, the name <i>Kalaallit Nunaat</i> was spelled <i>Kalãlit Nunât</i> or <i>Kalàlit Nunât</i>. This scheme uses the <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">circumflex</a> (◌̂) to indicate a long vowel (e.g. <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ât, ît, ût&#x27e9;</span>; modern: <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;aat, iit, uut&#x27e9;</span>), an <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">acute accent</a> (◌́) to indicate gemination of the following consonant: (i.e. <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ák, ík, úk&#x27e9;</span>; modern: <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;akk, ikk, ukk&#x27e9;</span>) and, finally, a <a href="/wiki/Tilde" title="Tilde">tilde</a> (◌̃) or a <a href="/wiki/Grave_accent" title="Grave accent">grave accent</a> (◌̀), depending on the author, indicates vowel length and gemination of the following consonant (e.g. <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ãt/àt, ĩt/ìt, ũt/ùt&#x27e9;</span>; modern: <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;aatt, iitt, uutt&#x27e9;</span>). <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ê, ô&#x27e9;</span>, used only before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;r, q&#x27e9;</span>, are now written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ee, oo&#x27e9;</span> in Greenlandic. The spelling system of <a href="/wiki/Nunatsiavummiutut" class="mw-redirect" title="Nunatsiavummiutut">Nunatsiavummiutut</a>, spoken in <a href="/wiki/Nunatsiavut" title="Nunatsiavut">Nunatsiavut</a> in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a>, is derived from the old Greenlandic system.
</p><p>Technically, the Kleinschmidt orthography focused upon <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphology</a>: the same derivational affix would be written in the same way in different contexts, despite its being pronounced differently in different contexts. The 1973 reform replaced this with a phonological system: Here, there was a clear link from written form to pronunciation, and the same suffix is now written differently in different contexts: for example <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e, o&#x27e9;</span> do not represent separate phonemes, but only more open pronunciations of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/q/</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁ/</span>. The differences are due to phonological changes. It is therefore easy to go from the old orthography to the new (cf. the online converter)<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> whereas going the other direction would require a full lexical analysis.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Example_text">Example text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Example text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> in Greenlandic:
</p><p>(Pre-reform)
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">Inuit tamarmik inúngorput nangminêrsivnâgsusseĸarlutik agsigĩmigdlo atarĸinagsusseĸarlutigdlo pisivnâtitãfeĸarlutik. Silaĸagsussermik tarnigdlo nalúngigsussianik pilerssugaugput, ingmingnudlo iliorfigeĸatigĩtariaĸaraluarput ĸatángutigĩtut peĸatigîvnerup anersâvane.</i></span></dd></dl>
<p>(Post-reform)
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">Inuit tamarmik inunngorput nammineersinnaassuseqarlutik assigiimmillu ataqqinassuseqarlutillu pisinnaatitaaffeqarlutik. Silaqassusermik tarnillu nalunngissusianik pilersugaapput, imminnullu iliorfigeqatigiittariaqaraluarput qatanngutigiittut peqatigiinnerup anersaavani.</i></span></dd></dl>
<p>Article 1 of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights in English:
</p>
<dl><dd>"All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood."</dd></dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The CIA <i>World Factbook</i> has reported Greenlandic literacy as being 100 percent since at least 2007, when it also reported six other countries achieving one hundred percent literacy.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Factbook</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s most recently reported data for Greenland literacy was for 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the Namminersornerullutik Oqartussat / Grønlands Hjemmestyres (Greenlands Home, official website): " <i>Language. The official languages are Greenlandic and Danish.... Greenlandic is the language [that is] used in schools and [that] dominates in most towns and settlements</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The uvular nasal <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɴ]</span> is not found in all dialects and there is dialectal variability regarding its status as a phoneme (Rischel 1974:176–181)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Short <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t͡s]</span> is in complementary distribution with short <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t]</span>, with the former appearing before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> and the latter elsewhere; both are written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;t&#x27e9;</span> and could be analysed as belonging to the same phoneme <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span>. Before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>, long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tt͡s]</span> occurs while long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tt]</span> does not, so long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tt͡s]</span> before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> could be analysed as long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tt/</span>. However, before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span>, both long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tt͡s]</span> and long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tt]</span> occur (except in some dialects, including that of Greenland's <a href="/wiki/Ilulissat" title="Ilulissat">third largest town</a>). Long <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tt͡s]</span> is always written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ts&#x27e9;</span>, e.g. <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">asavatsigut</i></span> ‘you love us’, <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">atsa</i></span> ‘aunt (father's sister)’, <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl"><a href="/wiki/Maniitsoq" title="Maniitsoq">Maniitsoq</a></i></span>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ff&#x27e9;</span> is the way of writing the devoiced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/vv/</span> <a href="/wiki/Geminate_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Geminate consonant">geminate</a>; <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rv/</span> is written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;rf&#x27e9;</span>; otherwise, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;f&#x27e9;</span> occurs only in loanwords.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">When <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l/</span> is geminated, it is heard as a <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɬɬ]</span> fricative sound.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> is found in some dialects (including those of Greenland's two largest towns) but is not distinguished from <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> in the written language.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example the word <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">Nalunaarasuartaatilioqateeraliorfinnialikkersaatiginialikkersaatilillaranatagoorunarsuarooq</i></span>, which means something like "Once again they tried to build a giant radio station, but it was apparently only on the drawing board".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">That can be compared to the English rate, of slightly more than one morpheme per word.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, the suffix with the shape <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">-aa</i></span> means "his/hers/its" when it is suffixed to a noun but "him/her/it" when it is suffixed to a verb. Likewise the suffix <span title="Greenlandic-language text"><i lang="kl">-ra</i></span> means "my" or "me", depending on whether it is suffixed on a verb or a noun.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abbreviations">Abbreviations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenlandic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Abbreviations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For affixes about which the precise meaning is the cause of discussion among specialists, the suffix itself is used as a gloss, and its meaning must be understood from context: -SSA (meaning either future or expectation), -NIKUU and -SIMA.
</p>
<div style="display:none;">
<p>4:fourth (reflexive or obviative) person
PART:participial mood
EQU:equative case
CONT:contemporative mood
INT:intransitive
INSTR:instrumental case
POSS:possessor
</p>
CAU:causative mood</div>
